# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# etcd MVCC Compaction and Watch Stream Cancellation

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in etcd-io/etcd that implement MVCC compaction: the compaction schedule (periodic vs revision-based), the compaction of revision indices, the notification of watch streams that span a compacted revision, and the slow watch detection.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

Perfect! I've completed the comprehensive analysis of MVCC compaction in etcd-io/etcd. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary of Findings

I've identified **12 key Go source files** that implement MVCC compaction and related watch stream functionality:

### Compaction Scheduling (2 files)
- **Periodic Compaction** (`server/etcdserver/api/v3compactor/periodic.go`): Time-based retention with revisions sampled every 1/10th of retention period
- **Revision Compaction** (`server/etcdserver/api/v3compactor/revision.go`): Revision-based retention, compacting every 5 minutes

### Compaction Execution (5 files)
- **kvstore.go**: `Compact()`, `updateCompactRev()`, `compact()` - main coordination methods
- **kvstore_compaction.go**: `scheduleCompaction()` - batch-by-batch deletion with sleep intervals
- **index.go**: Tree index compaction
- **key_index.go**: Per-key revision compaction
- **revision.go**: Revision type definitions (Main/Sub components)

### Watch Stream Management (3 files)
- **watchable_store.go**: `syncWatchers()` detects slow watchers, `notify()` sends events to synced watchers, `moveVictims()` retries slow consumers
- **watcher.go**: WatchResponse with CompactRevision field
- **watcher_group.go**: `chooseAll()` - **critical function** that detects watchers with minRev < compactionRev and sends them compaction notifications

### Slow Watcher Detection & Metrics (1 file)
- **metrics.go**: `slowWatcherGauge` tracks unsynced slow watchers

The analysis shows that etcd implements a sophisticated system where compaction is scheduled independently (periodic or revision-based), executed in batches to avoid blocking, and watch streams are notified via `WatchResponse{CompactRevision: compactRev}` when their revision falls behind the compaction point.

watchers from the unsynced watcher group\\n343: //  2. iterate over the set to get the minimum revision and remove compacted watchers\\n344: //  3. use minimum revision to get all key-value pairs and send those events to watchers\\n345: //  4. remove synced watchers in set from unsynced group and move to synced group\\n346: func (s *watchableStore) syncWatchers(evs []mvccpb.Event) (int, []mvccpb.Event) {\\n347: \\ts.mu.Lock()\\n348: \\tdefer s.mu.Unlock()\\n349: \\n350: \\tif s.unsynced.size() == 0 {\\n351: \\t\\treturn 0, []mvccpb.Event{}\\n352: \\t}\\n353: \\n354: \\ts.store.revMu.RLock()\\n355: \\tdefer s.store.revMu.RUnlock()\\n356: \\n357: \\t// in order to find key-value pairs from unsynced watchers, we need to\\n358: \\t// find min revision index, and \\n416: // rangeEventsWithReuse returns events in range [minRev, maxRev), while reusing already provided events.\\n417: func rangeEventsWithReuse(lg *zap.Logger, b backend.Backend, evs []mvccpb.Event, minRev, maxRev int64) []mvccpb.Event {\\n418: \\tif len(evs) == 0 {\\n419: \\t\\treturn rangeEvents(lg, b, minRev, maxRev)\\n420: \\t}\\n421: \\t// append from left\\n422: \\tif evs[0].Kv.ModRevision > minRev {\\n423: \\t\\tevs = append(rangeEvents(lg, b, minRev, evs[0].Kv.ModRevision), evs...)\\n424: \\t}\\n425: \\t// cut from left\\n426: \\tprefixIndex := 0\\n427: \\tfor prefixIndex < len(evs) \\t\\tsuffixIndex--\\n443: \\t}\\n444: \\tevs = evs[:suffixIndex+1]\\n445: \\treturn evs\\n446: }\\n447: \\n448: // rangeEvents returns events in range [minRev, maxRev).\\n449: func rangeEvents(lg *zap.Logger, b backend.Backend, minRev, maxRev int64) []mvccpb.Event {\\n450: \\tif minRev < 0 {\\n451: \\t\\tlg.Warn(\\\"Unexpected negative revision range start\\\", zap.Int64(\\\"minRev\\\", RevToBytes(Revision{Main: maxRev}, maxBytes)\\n457: \\n458: \\t// UnsafeRange returns keys and values. event at the given rev just happened to\\n491: // watchers that watch on the key of the event.\\n492: func (s *watchableStore) notify(rev int64, evs []mvccpb.Event) {\\n493: \\tvictim := COMPACTION SCHEDULING:\\n   - server/etcdserver/api/v3compactor/periodic.go: Implements periodic compaction scheduling (time-based retention). The Periodic.Run() method records revisions every 1/10th of the retention period and triggers compaction based on elapsed time. For example, with a 1-hour retention, it compacts every hour using revisions from 1 hour ago.\\n   - server/etcdserver/api/v3compactor/revision.go: Implements revision-based compaction scheduling. WATCH STREAM NOTIFICATION AND COMPACTION:\\n   - server/storage/mvcc/watchable_store.go:\\n     * syncWatchers(evs): Syncs unsynced watchers by selecting a batch (up to 512 watchers), fetching events between their minRev and current revision, and sending them events. Detects watchers with minRev < compactionRev and marks them for compaction notification.\\n     * notify(rev, evs): Sends events to synced watchers. If a watcher's channel is full (slow consumer), marks it as a victim.\\n     * moveVictims(): Periodically tries to send buffered responses to victim watchers that previously couldn't receive events.\\n     * syncWatchersLoop(): Runs every 100ms (watchResyncPeriod) to continuously sync unsynced watchers.\\n     * syncVictimsLoop(): Runs continuously to retry sending responses to slow watchers.\\n\\n4. SLOW WATCHER DETECTION:\\n   - server/storage/mvcc/watcher_group.go:\\n     * chooseAll(curRev, compactRev): Critical function that detects slow watchers. For each watcher, if w.minRev < compactRev, it sends a WatchResponse with CompactRevision set and marks the watcher as compacted (removing it from the group). This notifies the client that its watch was canceled due to compaction. If the notification channel is full (slow consumer), it retries later.\\n     * choose(maxWatchers, curRev, compactRev): Selects up to maxWatchers from the group and calls chooseAll to detect slow watchers and those affected by compaction.\\n\\n   - server/storage/mvcc/watchable_store.go lines 368-374:\\n     * When syncing unsynced watchers, if w.minRev < compactionRev, the watcher is skipped in this sync pass (already processed for compaction). This prevents duplicate notifications.\\n\\n   - server/storage/mvcc/metrics.go:\\n     * slowWatcherGauge: Prometheus gauge tracking the count of unsynced slow watchers. Incremented when watchers are moved to unsynced group or become victims. Decremented when they sync or are canceled.\\n     * Related metrics: dbCompactionTotalMs, dbCompactionPauseMs, indexCompactionPauseMs track compaction performance.\\n\\n5. BucketKey extends Revision with tombstone marking.\\n   - server/storage/mvcc/watcher.go: Defines WatchResponse with CompactRevision field (set when watcher is canceled due to compaction).\\n\\nThe overall flow: Compactors (periodic or revision-based) call Compact() \u2192 updateCompactRev() updates the revision to compact \u2192 compact() schedules a job \u2192 scheduleCompaction() deletes revisions in batches.
